المرصد السابع - المقصد الثالث : تسميته تعالى بالاسماء توفيقية
أما في القرآن فكالمولى والنصير والغالب والقاهر والقريب والرب والناصر والأعلى والأكرم وأحسن الخالقين وأرحم الراحمين وذي الطول وذي القوة وذي المعارج إلى غير ذلك . وأما في الحديث فكالحنان والمنّان، وقد ورد في رواية ابن ماجه أسماء ليست في الرواية المشهورة كالتام والقديم والوتر والشديد والكافي وغيرها، وإحصاؤها إما حفظها لأنه إنما يحصل بتكرار مجموعنا وتعدادها مراراً، وإما ضبطها حصراً وتعداداً وعلماً وإيماناً وقياماً بحقوقها. وبالجملة ( فلتخصها إحصاء) طمعاً في دخول الجنة . فنقول : ( الله ) وهو (اسم خاص بذاته لا يوصف به غيره ) أي لا يطلق على غيره أصلاً. ( فقيل : ) هو ( علم جامد ( لا اشتقاق له، وهو أحد قولي الخليل وسيبويه، والمروي عن أبي حنيفة والشافعي وأبي سليمان الخطابي والغزالي رحمهم الله تعالى. وقيل: مشتق وأصله الإله حذفت الهمزة لنقلها وأدغم اللام وهو من أله ) بفتح اللام أي عبد وهو المراد بقوله : (إذا تعبد . وقيل : ( الإله مأخوذ ( من الوله وهو الحيرة ومرجعهما صفة إضافية هي كونه معبوداً للخلائق ومختاراً للعقول . (وقيل: ) معنى الإله (هو ) بمعرفتها الأنبياء والأولياء ويحتمل الدخول لكنه مبهم لا يعرفه بعينه الأولى، ومنشأ الكرامات هو الدعاء به بخصوصه كذا ذكره الإمام الغزالي في شرح الأسماء الحسنى والحق أن التصرف بالاسم الأعظم وبأي اسم كان من أسماء التصرف موقوف على تحصيل المناسبة مع مسماه والتخلق بأخلاقه وبمجرد ذكر الاسم الأعظم لا يحصل المناسبة كما أن ذكر اسم السلطان لا ينفع ما لم يحصل معه المناسبة الخاصة اللهم انفعنا .
قوله : ( وأما في الحديث إلخ) اختلف في أنه له يجوز تسمية الله تعالى بما ثبت بخبر الواحدة فقيل: يجوز لأنه من باب العمل وقيل لا يجوز لأنه من باب الاعتقاد ثم الظاهر أن الإطلاق وإن كان جه الإخبار يكفي في الأذن ما لم يكن في السوق أمر آخر يمنعه وإلا يلزم أن لا يكون كثير من الأسماء مأذونة فلا عبرة بما في شرح المشارق من أنه لا يلزم من قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها أن الله رفيق يحب الرفق صحة أن يقال : يا رفيق لأنه ذكر على وجه الإخبار . قوله: (فكالحنان) هو بالتشديد من الحنان بالتخفيف وهو الرحمة قال الله تعالى وحناناً من لدنا ﴾ [مريم : ۱۳] .

The Seventh Observation Post - Third Objective: Naming Allah with Names is Tawfiqi (Based on Revelation). The Meaning of Ilah and the Greatest Name
Explains the meaning of Ilah and the conditions for the Greatest Name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological implications of the word 'Ilah' and the conditions for benefiting from the Greatest Name.

Core Idea
Benefiting from the Greatest Name requires spiritual suitability, not mere uttering.

This lesson delves deeper into the meaning of 'Ilah' and introduces the concept of the Greatest Name of Allah. It explains that true benefit from the divine names depends on attaining harmony with God's attributes, not just reciting words.

Guided Path
1
Read about 'Ilah'
Understand that 'Ilah' is associated with being known by prophets and awliya.
2
Understand the Greatest Name
The passage discusses the Greatest Name and its relation to karamat (miracles).
It emphasizes that mere mention is not sufficient.
3
Grasp the condition of suitability
The key is to have munasaba (suitability) with the Named by adopting His attributes.
This is likened to approaching a sultan: mere mention of his name does not give access.

And it is said: It is a frozen proper noun (علم جامد) with no derivation, and this is one of the two opinions of Khalil and Sibawayh, and narrated from Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi, and al-Ghazali, may Allah have mercy on them. And it is said: It is derived, and its original is al-Ilah, the hamza was deleted due to transmission and the lam was merged, and it is from alaha (with fatha on lam), i.e., to worship, and this is what is meant by His saying: 'when one worshipped'. And it is said: al-Ilah is taken from al-walah which is confusion, and the return of both is an added attribute (sifa idafiyya) which is that He is worshipped by creatures and chosen by intellects. And it is said: the meaning of al-Ilah is the one known by the prophets and awliya, and it is possible to enter but it is ambiguous not known specifically by the first, and the source of karamat is supplication with it specifically, as mentioned by Imam al-Ghazali in Sharh al-Asma' al-Husna. And the truth is that the disposal by the Greatest Name and by any name of the names of disposal is dependent on attaining suitability (munasaba) with its named and adopting His attributes, and merely mentioning the Greatest Name does not achieve suitability, just as mentioning the name of a sultan does not benefit unless there is a special suitability with him. O Allah, benefit us.
His saying: 'As for in the Hadith etc.' There is disagreement about whether it is permissible to name Allah with what is established by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid). It is said: It is permissible because it is a matter of action. And it is said: It is not permissible because it is a matter of belief. Then the apparent view is that the use, even if it is in the manner of informing, suffices for permission as long as there is no other matter that prevents it. Otherwise, it would necessitate that many names are not permitted. So no consideration is given to what is in Sharh al-Mashariq that it does not follow from the saying of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, that Allah is kind and loves kindness, the correctness of saying 'O Kind One', because it was mentioned as information.
His saying: 'such as al-Hannan' is with tashdid from al-hannan with takhiff, which is mercy. Allah said: 'and kindness from Us' (19:13).
His saying: 'and this is one of the two opinions of Khalil and Sibawayh.' Ibn Jinni narrated that Sibawayh was seen in a dream and it was said: 'What did Allah do with you?' He said: 'Good.' And he mentioned a great miracle. It was said to him: 'How did you attain that?' He said: 'Because I said that Allah is the most known of known things.'
The name: His saying: 'and its original is al-Ilah' - it is possible that the definite article therein is from the narrated (al-mahki), which is the apparent from the words of the commentator, and it is possible that it is from the anecdote (al-hikaya), such that the original was indefinite. And each group has adopted [a view]. His saying: 'from al-walah' - so 'Ilaah' on both views is fu'ala in the sense of maf'ul, but on the second its original is 'walah', the waw was replaced by hamza as they said in 'wisad' to 'asadd'.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage defines the name 'Allah' and discusses whether it is a derived or frozen proper noun. It begins by stating the principle that divine names are tawfiqi (based on revelation). Then it gives examples of names in the Quran and Hadith, and also mentions names found in Ibn Majah's narration. It emphasizes the importance of enumerating (ihsa') the names. Then it focuses on the name 'Allah', defining it as a name specific to God's essence, not applied to others. It presents two main opinions: (1) it is a frozen proper noun (علم جامد) with no derivation, attributed to Khalil, Sibawayh, Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, al-Khattabi, and al-Ghazali; (2) it is derived from al-Ilah, which itself comes from the root 'alaha' meaning to worship, or from 'walah' meaning confusion. The passage then discusses the meaning of 'Ilah' as an added attribute of being worshipped. It also includes a note from al-Ghazali about the Greatest Name and the need for spiritual suitability. The passage ends with a remark about Sibawayh's dream and a grammatical note on the derivation.

Naming Allah from Solitary Reports and Grammatical Notes
Discusses the permissibility of naming Allah from solitary reports and grammatical notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on using names from solitary hadith reports and the grammatical analysis of 'al-Ilah'.

Core Idea
Names from solitary reports are permissible, and the grammar of 'al-Ilah' has subtle implications.

This lesson concludes the discussion by addressing a legal question: can we use names for Allah that are proven only by solitary hadith? It also provides a grammatical note on the definite article in 'al-Ilah' and an anecdote about Sibawayh's dream.

Guided Path
1
Understand the disagreement
Note the two opinions on naming Allah from solitary reports: one says it's permissible (action), another says no (belief).
2
Prefer the permissive view
The passage seems to prefer the permissive view, as long as there is no other impediment.
It criticizes a contrary opinion from Sharh al-Mashariq.
3
Grammatical note on 'al-Ilah'
The passage discusses whether the definite article in 'al-Ilah' is from the narrated or anecdotal form.
This is a technical point for advanced students.
4
Sibawayh's dream
The dream anecdote emphasizes the importance of correct belief about Allah's names.
Sibawayh attributed his reward to his correct understanding.

The Name 'Allah': From Description to Proper Name
Introduces tawqif and the name 'Allah' with its transformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the name 'Allah' is considered a proper name that indicates perfect attributes through common usage, and the principle of tawqif in divine naming.

Core Idea
The name 'Allah' encodes all perfect attributes by divine appointment.

This lesson introduces the principle that divine names are tawqifi (based on revelation) and explains how the name 'Allah' originally a description became a proper name that still signifies all perfections. This foundation is essential for understanding the subsequent names.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on tawqif and the name 'Allah'
Read the Arabic and translation of the first paragraph, which discusses the tawqifi nature and the transformation of 'Allah' from a description to a proper name.
2
Understand the three variant interpretations of the root meaning
The passage lists three possible original meanings of the word 'Allah': the Powerful, the one who wills, and the one from whom taklif proceeds. Note how each returns to an attribute (power, will, or negative/active).
3
Grasp the conclusion about the name 'Allah'
Despite being originally a description, the word 'Allah' became a proper name by common usage, yet it still indicates all perfect attributes. This is similar to nicknames that imply qualities.

( المهيمن) أي (الشاهد ، وفسر) كونه شاهداً تارة ( بالعلم) فيرجع إلى صفة العلم (و) أخرى ( بالتصديق بالقول ( فيرجع إلى صفة كلامية . وقيل : ) معنى المهيمن (الأمين أي الصادق في قوله فيكون صفة كلامية. وقيل: هو بمعنى الحفيظ

The Seventh Observation Post - Third Objective: Naming Allah with Names is Tawfiqi. (Page 235) The Powerful over creation, so it returns to the attribute of power (qudra). And it is said: He is the one that nothing happens except what He wills. And it is said: He is the one from whom alone obligation (taklif) is valid. So its return on these two faces is a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) and an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya). And the correct view is that the word 'Allah' on the assumption that it was originally a description has been transformed into a proper name indicating perfect attributes due to common usage (al-ishtihar).
(Al-Rahman, al-Rahim): the two are like the synonyms (al-nadman) and the intimate friend (al-nadim). i.e., the one who intends bestowal of blessings on creation, so their return is the attribute of will (irada). And it is said: the giver of great blessings and their details, so the return then is an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya).
(Al-Malik): i.e., He honors whom He wills and disgraces whom He wills, and none can humiliate Him, i.e., His humiliation is impossible. So its return is an active and negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is complete power, so its return is the attribute of power (qudra).
(Al-Quddus): i.e., the one free from defects. And it is said: He is the one whom imaginations and eyesights do not perceive, so it is a negative attribute on both views.
(Al-Salam): i.e., the one possessing safety from deficiencies absolutely in His essence, attributes, and actions, so it is a negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is from Him and by Him is safety, i.e., He is the giver of safety in the beginning and the end, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: He greets His creation. Allah said: 'Peace, a word from a Merciful Lord' (36:58), so it is an attribute of speech (sifa kalamiyya).
(Al-Mu'min): He is the one who confirms Himself in what He has informed about, like oneness, e.g., His saying: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He', and His messenger in what they informed about in their conveying from Him - either by speech, like His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', so it is an attribute of speech; or He creates the miracle indicating the truthfulness of messengers and the creation of the world in the observed order indicating oneness, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is the one who gives security to His believing servants from the greatest terror - either by His act and creating security and tranquility in them, so it returns to an active attribute; or by His informing them of security from that, so it is an attribute of speech.
(Al-Muhaymin): i.e., the witness. And His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge; and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it is said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is the trustworthy, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it is said: it is in the sense of the protector (al-hafiz).
His saying: 'due to common usage (lishtihar)' - it is said: there is no impossibility in it indicating some [perfections] considering the origin, as in nicknames and titles.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage explains the meanings and classifications of several divine names: al-Rahman, al-Rahim, al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin. For each name, it provides a definition and classifies it as referring to an attribute of essence (like power, will, knowledge), an attribute of action (like giving blessings, honoring/disgracing), a negative attribute (like being free from defects), or an attribute of speech. For example, al-Rahman and al-Rahim are said to refer to the attribute of will (irada) as they indicate intention to bestow blessings, but they can also be active attributes if interpreted as giving. Al-Malik combines active (giving honor/disgrace) and negative (none can humiliate Him) attributes. Al-Quddus is purely negative. Al-Salam has multiple interpretations: negative (free from deficiencies), active (giving safety), or speech (saying 'peace'). Al-Mu'min confirms truthfulness, either through speech or through creating miracles, so it can be speech or action. Al-Muhaymin means witness, which can be through knowledge or speech. The passage also includes a concluding note about the name 'Allah' indicating perfect attributes due to common usage, like a nickname that implies qualities.

Key Terms
توفيقية
صفة سلبية
صفة فعلية
لفظة الله
للاشتهار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine names can be freely invented or derived from human reason alone.
Correction: The passage asserts that naming Allah is tawqifi (based on divine disclosure), not arbitrary.

Checkpoint
What is the correct view about the name 'Allah' according to the passage?
A) It is a pure description with no proper name status.
B) It was originally a description but became a proper name indicating perfect attributes.
C) It is a name with no meaning at all.
D) It is derived from human opinion and common usage alone.

Key Takeaway
The name 'Allah' is a proper name that, despite its origin as a description, now signifies all perfect attributes by divine appointment and common usage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you utter the name 'Allah' in your daily prayers, do you consciously reflect that it encodes every perfect attribute, or has it become a mere label? What would it take to transform your invocation into a living recognition of His perfection?
?
This lesson says the name 'Allah' originally described power or will. Do you treat Allah as the Powerful One in your moments of weakness, and the Willing One when you surrender your plans? Or do you live as if His power is distant?
?
If the name 'Allah' is tawqifi – divinely appointed – then how carefully do you use it? Do you ever invoke Him casually, forgetting that this name is a gift and a command to know Him truly? What will you change in how you say His name starting today?

Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim: The Merciful
Explains the meanings and classifications of Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim and how they relate to the attributes of will or action.

Core Idea
Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim both indicate mercy, but their classification differs by interpretation.

This lesson delves into the paired names Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim. The passage explains that they indicate the intention to bestow blessings (thus referring to will) or the actual giving of great and subtle blessings (thus referring to action). This shows how a single name can have multiple valid interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim
Read the Arabic and translation for these two names. Note that they are treated together as synonyms.
2
Identify the two interpretations
First interpretation: they mean the one who intends to bestow blessings (returns to will). Second: the giver of great and subtle blessings (returns to active attribute). Understand the difference.
3
Reflect on the implications
Notice that both names are derived from the same root (r-h-m) but can be understood in different ways. This shows the richness of divine names.

The Seventh Observation Post - Third Objective: Naming Allah with Names is Tawfiqi. (Page 235) The Powerful over creation, so it returns to the attribute of power (qudra). And it is said: He is the one that nothing happens except what He wills. And it is said: He is the one from whom alone obligation (taklif) is valid. So its return on these two faces is a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) and an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya). And the correct view is that the word 'Allah' on the assumption that it was originally a description has been transformed into a proper name indicating perfect attributes due to common usage (al-ishtihar).
(Al-Rahman, al-Rahim): the two are like the synonyms (al-nadman) and the intimate friend (al-nadim). i.e., the one who intends bestowal of blessings on creation, so their return is the attribute of will (irada). And it is said: the giver of great blessings and their details, so the return then is an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya).
(Al-Malik): i.e., He honors whom He wills and disgraces whom He wills, and none can humiliate Him, i.e., His humiliation is impossible. So its return is an active and negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is complete power, so its return is the attribute of power (qudra).
(Al-Quddus): i.e., the one free from defects. And it is said: He is the one whom imaginations and eyesights do not perceive, so it is a negative attribute on both views.
(Al-Salam): i.e., the one possessing safety from deficiencies absolutely in His essence, attributes, and actions, so it is a negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is from Him and by Him is safety, i.e., He is the giver of safety in the beginning and the end, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: He greets His creation. Allah said: 'Peace, a word from a Merciful Lord' (36:58), so it is an attribute of speech (sifa kalamiyya).
(Al-Mu'min): He is the one who confirms Himself in what He has informed about, like oneness, e.g., His saying: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He', and His messenger in what they informed about in their conveying from Him - either by speech, like His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', so it is an attribute of speech; or He creates the miracle indicating the truthfulness of messengers and the creation of the world in the observed order indicating oneness, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is the one who gives security to His believing servants from the greatest terror - either by His act and creating security and tranquility in them, so it returns to an active attribute; or by His informing them of security from that, so it is an attribute of speech.
(Al-Muhaymin): i.e., the witness. And His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge; and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it is said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is the trustworthy, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it is said: it is in the sense of the protector (al-hafiz).
His saying: 'due to common usage (lishtihar)' - it is said: there is no impossibility in it indicating some [perfections] considering the origin, as in nicknames and titles.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage explains the meanings and classifications of several divine names: al-Rahman, al-Rahim, al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin. For each name, it provides a definition and classifies it as referring to an attribute of essence (like power, will, knowledge), an attribute of action (like giving blessings, honoring/disgracing), a negative attribute (like being free from defects), or an attribute of speech. For example, al-Rahman and al-Rahim are said to refer to the attribute of will (irada) as they indicate intention to bestow blessings, but they can also be active attributes if interpreted as giving. Al-Malik combines active (giving honor/disgrace) and negative (none can humiliate Him) attributes. Al-Quddus is purely negative. Al-Salam has multiple interpretations: negative (free from deficiencies), active (giving safety), or speech (saying 'peace'). Al-Mu'min confirms truthfulness, either through speech or through creating miracles, so it can be speech or action. Al-Muhaymin means witness, which can be through knowledge or speech. The passage also includes a concluding note about the name 'Allah' indicating perfect attributes due to common usage, like a nickname that implies qualities.

الرحيم
صفة الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim are synonymous without any nuance in attributes.
Correction: The passage shows that depending on interpretation, these names can refer to either the attribute of will (irada) or an active attribute (fi'liyya).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, to which attribute do Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim return when interpreted as meaning 'the one who intends bestowal of blessings'?
A) Power (qudra)
B) Will (irada)
C) Knowledge (ilm)
D) Speech (kalam)

Key Takeaway
Al-Rahman and Al-Rahim indicate divine mercy, either as an intention (will) or as an act (giving blessings).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah as Al-Rahman, do you focus more on His intention to be merciful or on the actual blessings you receive? Which focus deepens your trust in Him right now? Commit to one specific way you will remember His mercy today.
?
The passage presents two scholarly views on the same names. Which view resonates more with your current relationship with Allah—are you more aware of His will to bless you or His actual provisions? How does that affect your gratitude when blessings are delayed?
?
If mercy is both an intention and an act, how does that challenge your impatience when you don't see immediate results? Will you choose to believe in His will to be merciful even when the act is not yet visible? What one step can you take today to act on that belief?

Al-Malik: The Sovereign
Explains the meaning and classification of Al-Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Al-Malik and how it combines active and negative attributes.

Core Idea
Al-Malik signifies sovereignty that honors and humbles, while being immune to humiliation.

This lesson explains the name Al-Malik, which means the one who gives honor and disgrace as He wills, and cannot be humiliated. This combines an active attribute (giving honor/disgrace) with a negative attribute (immunity from humiliation). An alternative interpretation ties it to complete power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Al-Malik
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two interpretations provided.
2
Analyze the first interpretation
Al-Malik means He honors whom He wills and disgraces whom He wills, and none can humiliate Him. This yields an active attribute (honoring/disgracing) and a negative attribute (impossibility of humiliation).
3
Consider the second interpretation
Another view says Al-Malik means complete power, thus returning to the attribute of qudra (power).

Al-Quddus: The All-Holy
Explains the meaning and negative classification of Al-Quddus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning and purely negative classification of the name Al-Quddus.

Core Idea
Al-Quddus means absolute purity, a negative attribute.

This lesson covers Al-Quddus, which means the one free from all defects. The passage gives two definitions: being free from defects and being beyond perception. Both lead to a negative attribute, emphasizing Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Al-Quddus
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that there are two definitions.
2
Understand the two definitions
First definition: free from defects. Second definition: not perceived by imaginations and eyesights. Both are negative attributes.
3
Recognize the classification
Both definitions result in a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya). This shows that Al-Quddus is purely transcendent.

المرصد السابع - المقصد الثالث : تسميته تعالى بالاسماء توفيقية
٢٣٥
القادر على الخلق فيرجع إلى صفة القدرة . وقيل : هو الذي لا يكون إلا مايريد ( وقيل : من لا يصح التكليف إلا منه . فمرجعه على هذين الوجهين (صفة سلبية ) ( فعلية. والصحيح أن لفظة الله على تقدير كونها في الأصل صفة فقد انقلبت علماً مشعراً بصفات الكمال للاشتهار (الرحمن) (الرحيم هما بمنزلة الندمان، والنديم ( أي مريد الإنعام على الخلق فمرجعهما صفة الإرادة . وقيل : معطي جلائل النعم ودقائقها فالمرجع حينئذ صفة فعلية ( الملك ) أي ( يعز) من يشاء ( ويذل ) من يشاء ) ولا يذل أي يمتنع إذلاله ( فمرجعه صفة فعلية وسلبية وقيل : معناه التام القدرة فصفة القدرة ) مرجعه (القدوس) أي ( المبرأ عن المعايب ، وقيل :) هو الذي لا يدركه الأوهام والأبصار فصفة سلبية ) على الوجهين (السلام) أي (ذو السلامة عن النقائص) مطلقاً في ذاته وصفاته وأفعاله ( فصفة سلبية ، وقيل : ( معناه منه وبه السلامة ) أي هو المعطي للسلامة في المبدأ والمعاد ( ففعلية . وقيل : يسلم على خلقه، قال تعالى: سلام قولا من رب رحيم ﴾ [يس:٥٨]، فصفة كلامية المؤمن ) هو ( المصدق لنفسه ) فيما أخبر به كالوحدانية مثلا في قوله : شهد الله أنه لا إله إلا هو ( ورسوله) فيما أخبروا به في تبليغهم عنه ( إما بالقول ) نحو قوله تعالى : محمد رسول الله ( فصفة كلامية أو يخلق المعجز الدال على صدق الرسل وخلق العالم على النظام المشاهد الدال على الوحدانية ( ففعلية . وقيل : ) معناه (المؤمن لعباده المؤمنين ( من الفزع الأكبر إما بفعله) وإيجاده (الأمن) والطمأنينة فيهم فيرجع إلى صفة فعلية ( أو بإخباره( إياهم بالأمن من ذلك فيكون صفة كلامية. ( المهيمن) أي (الشاهد ، وفسر) كونه شاهداً تارة ( بالعلم) فيرجع إلى صفة العلم (و) أخرى ( بالتصديق بالقول ( فيرجع إلى صفة كلامية . وقيل : ) معنى المهيمن (الأمين أي الصادق في قوله فيكون صفة كلامية. وقيل: هو بمعنى الحفيظ
(
قوله: (للاشتهار) قيل : لا بعد في أن يشعر بالبعض باعتبار ملاحظة الأصل كما في الكنى
والألقاب .
The Seventh Observation Post - Third Objective: Naming Allah with Names is Tawfiqi. (Page 235) The Powerful over creation, so it returns to the attribute of power (qudra). And it is said: He is the one that nothing happens except what He wills. And it is said: He is the one from whom alone obligation (taklif) is valid. So its return on these two faces is a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) and an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya). And the correct view is that the word 'Allah' on the assumption that it was originally a description has been transformed into a proper name indicating perfect attributes due to common usage (al-ishtihar).
(Al-Rahman, al-Rahim): the two are like the synonyms (al-nadman) and the intimate friend (al-nadim). i.e., the one who intends bestowal of blessings on creation, so their return is the attribute of will (irada). And it is said: the giver of great blessings and their details, so the return then is an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya).
(Al-Malik): i.e., He honors whom He wills and disgraces whom He wills, and none can humiliate Him, i.e., His humiliation is impossible. So its return is an active and negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is complete power, so its return is the attribute of power (qudra).
(Al-Quddus): i.e., the one free from defects. And it is said: He is the one whom imaginations and eyesights do not perceive, so it is a negative attribute on both views.
(Al-Salam): i.e., the one possessing safety from deficiencies absolutely in His essence, attributes, and actions, so it is a negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is from Him and by Him is safety, i.e., He is the giver of safety in the beginning and the end, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: He greets His creation. Allah said: 'Peace, a word from a Merciful Lord' (36:58), so it is an attribute of speech (sifa kalamiyya).
(Al-Mu'min): He is the one who confirms Himself in what He has informed about, like oneness, e.g., His saying: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He', and His messenger in what they informed about in their conveying from Him - either by speech, like His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', so it is an attribute of speech; or He creates the miracle indicating the truthfulness of messengers and the creation of the world in the observed order indicating oneness, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is the one who gives security to His believing servants from the greatest terror - either by His act and creating security and tranquility in them, so it returns to an active attribute; or by His informing them of security from that, so it is an attribute of speech.
(Al-Muhaymin): i.e., the witness. And His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge; and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it is said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is the trustworthy, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it is said: it is in the sense of the protector (al-hafiz).
His saying: 'due to common usage (lishtihar)' - it is said: there is no impossibility in it indicating some [perfections] considering the origin, as in nicknames and titles.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage explains the meanings and classifications of several divine names: al-Rahman, al-Rahim, al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin. For each name, it provides a definition and classifies it as referring to an attribute of essence (like power, will, knowledge), an attribute of action (like giving blessings, honoring/disgracing), a negative attribute (like being free from defects), or an attribute of speech. For example, al-Rahman and al-Rahim are said to refer to the attribute of will (irada) as they indicate intention to bestow blessings, but they can also be active attributes if interpreted as giving. Al-Malik combines active (giving honor/disgrace) and negative (none can humiliate Him) attributes. Al-Quddus is purely negative. Al-Salam has multiple interpretations: negative (free from deficiencies), active (giving safety), or speech (saying 'peace'). Al-Mu'min confirms truthfulness, either through speech or through creating miracles, so it can be speech or action. Al-Muhaymin means witness, which can be through knowledge or speech. The passage also includes a concluding note about the name 'Allah' indicating perfect attributes due to common usage, like a nickname that implies qualities.

Key Terms
القدوس
صفة سلبية
المعايب
الأوهام والأبصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Quddus implies a positive quality like holiness in a human sense.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Al-Quddus is a negative attribute, negating defects and limitations, not affirming a positive quality.

Checkpoint
How is Al-Quddus classified according to the passage?
A) Active attribute
B) Attribute of speech
C) Negative attribute
D) Attribute of power

Key Takeaway
Al-Quddus is a negative attribute signifying Allah's absolute purity and transcendence beyond defects and perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah, do you ever subconsciously imagine Him with human-like qualities or limitations? How does knowing that Al-Quddus means He is free from all defects force you to purify your concept of Him?
?
Your imagination and eyesight cannot perceive Allah. Have you ever tried to picture Allah in your mind? How should this truth change the way you relate to Him in your daily devotions?
?
If Allah is absolutely pure and beyond all defects, what does that demand from you in terms of your own purity and actions? Are there areas in your life where you are not striving to reflect His holiness? Commit to one specific change today.

Divine Attributes
beginner

Al-Salam: The Source of Peace
Explains the three interpretations of Al-Salam and their classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations of Al-Salam and their classifications: negative, active, or speech.

Core Idea
Al-Salam can mean safety from defects, giver of safety, or the one who greets.

This lesson examines the name Al-Salam, which has multiple layers. It can refer to being free from deficiencies (negative), giving safety (active), or uttering peace as a word (speech). This shows how one name can be understood under different attribute categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Al-Salam
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the three interpretations.
2
Identify the first interpretation
Al-Salam means possessing safety from deficiencies in essence, attributes, and actions – a negative attribute.
3
Identify the second and third interpretations
Second: He is the giver of safety (active). Third: He greets creation with 'Peace' (speech attribute).
The third interpretation is supported by Quran 36:58.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is absolutely free from all deficiencies (ذو السلامة عن النقائص), what does that reveal about the flaws you see in yourself? In what area of your life are you still relying on imperfect creations rather than Him for safety? Commit today to turn to Him alone in that area.
?
When you greet others with 'assalamu alaikum', do you realize you are invoking an attribute of Allah? How often do you say it without awareness? Starting today, before you greet anyone, pause and remember that you are echoing His attribute of speech. How will that change your interactions?
?
The Quran says from Allah is 'peace, a word from a Merciful Lord'. Have you ever truly received His peace in your heart? What sin or worry steals that peace from you? Go to Him now in prayer and ask for the salam that only He can give.

Al-Mu'min: The Giver of Security
Explains the meanings and classifications of Al-Mu'min

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Al-Mu'min and how it can be an attribute of speech or action.

Core Idea
Al-Mu'min confirms truth through speech or through creating miracles.

This lesson explains Al-Mu'min, which means the one who confirms His own truth and that of His messengers. This confirmation can be through speech (direct statements) or through action (creating miracles and the orderly universe). An additional interpretation relates to giving security to believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Al-Mu'min
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the multiple possibilities.
2
Understand the primary meaning: confirming truth
Al-Mu'min confirms Himself (oneness) and His messengers. This confirmation is either by speech (e.g., Quranic verses) or by action (creating miracles and the universe).
3
Consider the secondary meaning: giving security
Another view: Al-Mu'min gives security to believers from the greatest terror, either by creating safety (action) or by informing them (speech).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد السابع - المقصد الثالث : تسميته تعالى بالاسماء توفيقية

(Al-Muhaymin): i.e., the witness. And His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge; and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it is said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is the trustworthy, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it is said: it is in the sense of the protector (al-hafiz).
His saying: 'due to common usage (lishtihar)' - it is said: there is no impossibility in it indicating some [perfections] considering the origin, as in nicknames and titles.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage explains the meanings and classifications of several divine names: al-Rahman, al-Rahim, al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin. For each name, it provides a definition and classifies it as referring to an attribute of essence (like power, will, knowledge), an attribute of action (like giving blessings, honoring/disgracing), a negative attribute (like being free from defects), or an attribute of speech. For example, al-Rahman and al-Rahim are said to refer to the attribute of will (irada) as they indicate intention to bestow blessings, but they can also be active attributes if interpreted as giving. Al-Malik combines active (giving honor/disgrace) and negative (none can humiliate Him) attributes. Al-Quddus is purely negative. Al-Salam has multiple interpretations: negative (free from deficiencies), active (giving safety), or speech (saying 'peace'). Al-Mu'min confirms truthfulness, either through speech or through creating miracles, so it can be speech or action. Al-Muhaymin means witness, which can be through knowledge or speech. The passage also includes a concluding note about the name 'Allah' indicating perfect attributes due to common usage, like a nickname that implies qualities.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Mu'min means that Allah has faith (iman) like humans do.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Al-Mu'min means 'the one who confirms' (musaddiq) or 'the one who gives security' (mu'min), not 'the one who believes'.

D) By giving them power

Key Takeaway
Al-Mu'min means the one who confirms truth (through speech or action) and gives security (through action or speech).

?
If Al-Mu'min confirms truth both by speech (Quran) and by action (creation), which of these evidences resonates more deeply with you right now? What would it take for you to let go of a doubt and fully submit?

Al-Muhaymin: The Watchful Witness
Explains the meanings and classifications of Al-Muhaymin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Al-Muhaymin and its possible returns to knowledge, speech, or action.

Core Idea
Al-Muhaymin means the witness, which can be through knowledge or speech.

This final lesson covers Al-Muhaymin, meaning the witness or the protector. The passage gives several interpretations: He is the witness, which can be through knowledge (returning to knowledge) or through speech (confirming by saying). Another interpretation says He is the trustworthy or the truthful in speech, and yet another says He is the protector.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Al-Muhaymin
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the variety of interpretations.
2
Understand the primary meaning: witness
Al-Muhaymin means the witness. This can be interpreted as knowledge (scientific) or as confirmation by speech (kalam).
3
Consider the additional meanings
Other views: He is the trustworthy (truthful in speech) – speech attribute; or He is the protector (hafiz) – active attribute.

The Seventh Observation Post - Third Objective: Naming Allah with Names is Tawfiqi. (Page 235) The Powerful over creation, so it returns to the attribute of power (qudra). And it is said: He is the one that nothing happens except what He wills. And it is said: He is the one from whom alone obligation (taklif) is valid. So its return on these two faces is a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) and an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya). And the correct view is that the word 'Allah' on the assumption that it was originally a description has been transformed into a proper name indicating perfect attributes due to common usage (al-ishtihar).
(Al-Rahman, al-Rahim): the two are like the synonyms (al-nadman) and the intimate friend (al-nadim). i.e., the one who intends bestowal of blessings on creation, so their return is the attribute of will (irada). And it is said: the giver of great blessings and their details, so the return then is an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya).
(Al-Malik): i.e., He honors whom He wills and disgraces whom He wills, and none can humiliate Him, i.e., His humiliation is impossible. So its return is an active and negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is complete power, so its return is the attribute of power (qudra).
(Al-Quddus): i.e., the one free from defects. And it is said: He is the one whom imaginations and eyesights do not perceive, so it is a negative attribute on both views.
(Al-Salam): i.e., the one possessing safety from deficiencies absolutely in His essence, attributes, and actions, so it is a negative attribute. And it is said: its meaning is from Him and by Him is safety, i.e., He is the giver of safety in the beginning and the end, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: He greets His creation. Allah said: 'Peace, a word from a Merciful Lord' (36:58), so it is an attribute of speech (sifa kalamiyya).
(Al-Mu'min): He is the one who confirms Himself in what He has informed about, like oneness, e.g., His saying: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He', and His messenger in what they informed about in their conveying from Him - either by speech, like His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', so it is an attribute of speech; or He creates the miracle indicating the truthfulness of messengers and the creation of the world in the observed order indicating oneness, so it is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is the one who gives security to His believing servants from the greatest terror - either by His act and creating security and tranquility in them, so it returns to an active attribute; or by His informing them of security from that, so it is an attribute of speech.
(Al-Muhaymin): i.e., the witness. And His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge; and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it is said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is the trustworthy, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it is said: it is in the sense of the protector (al-hafiz).
His saying: 'due to common usage (lishtihar)' - it is said: there is no impossibility in it indicating some [perfections] considering the origin, as in nicknames and titles.

Commentary
This passage explains the meanings and classifications of several divine names: al-Rahman, al-Rahim, al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin. For each name, it provides a definition and classifies it as referring to an attribute of essence (like power, will, knowledge), an attribute of action (like giving blessings, honoring/disgracing), a negative attribute (like being free from defects), or an attribute of speech. Al-Mu'min confirms truthfulness, either through speech or through creating miracles, so it can be speech or action. Al-Muhaymin means witness, which can be through knowledge or speech. The passage also includes a concluding note about the name 'Allah' indicating perfect attributes due to common usage, like a nickname that implies qualities.

Divine Names and Their Attribute Categories (Part 1): al-Qadir to al-Rahim
Principle of tawqifiyya and definitions of first four names with attribute references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that divine names are based on revelation (tawqifiyya) and how the names al-Qadir, Allah, al-Rahman, and al-Rahim relate to attributes of power, will, or action.

Core Idea
Divine names are not arbitrary; each name reveals a specific divine attribute.

This lesson opens with a key principle: naming God is based on revelation, not human speculation. Then it examines the first four names—al-Qadir, Allah, al-Rahman, and al-Rahim—showing how scholars trace each back to an attribute of essence, will, or action. A marginal note further clarifies the nuanced difference between al-Rahman and al-Rahim.

Guided Path
1
Understand tawqifiyya
Read the opening statement that naming God is 'tawqifiyya' (based on revelation). This sets the ground for the entire discussion.
Without this principle, the rest of the passage would not follow.
2
Analyze al-Qadir
Notice how al-Qadir (the Powerful) is traced to the attribute of power (qudra), with alternative interpretations that also involve negation (salbiyya) and action (fi'liyya).
3
Examine the name 'Allah'
See how the word 'Allah' originally a description became a proper name symbolizing all perfections. The marginal note explains that this shift is like nicknames that still hint at their original meaning.
4
Study al-Rahman and al-Rahim
Read how both names refer to mercy, but are classified as either will (irada) or action (fi'liyya). Then study the marginal note comparing their comprehensiveness and usage.
This shows that even closely related names have distinct theological meanings.

قوله: (الرحمن الرحيم الرحمن أبلغ من الرحيم لما فيه من زيادة البناء فبعضهم الأبلغية باعتبار الكمية كما قيل : يا رحمن الدنيا ورحيم الآخرة لأن رحمة الدنيا تعم المؤمن والكافر ورحمة الآخرة تختص بالمؤمن، وبعضهم لاحظ الأبلغية باعتبار الكيفية فحمل الرحمن على المنعم بالنعم الأخروية لأنها كلها ،أجسام وأما النعم الدنيوية فحقيرة بالنسبة إليها وقيل: الرحيم أبلغ لأن الفعيل يكون للصفات الجبلية، وهو مردود بالسقيم والمريض ثم الرحمن من الصفات الغالبة لم يستعمل في غير الله تعالى، ولهذا قدم على الرحيم وقول بني حنيفة لمسيلمة الكذاب : رحمن اليمامة تعنت وتمرد .
The seventh observatory - the third purpose: Naming Him, exalted, with names is based on revelation (tawqifiyya). The Powerful over creation, so it returns to the attribute of power (qudra). And it was said: He is the one who only what He wills occurs. And it was said: He from whom valid obligation (taklif) is only from Him. So its reference in these two aspects is a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) and an attribute of action (sifa fi'liyya). And the correct view is that the word 'Allah', on the assumption that it was originally a description, has turned into a proper name (علم) indicating attributes of perfection due to widespread usage. (Al-Rahman) (Al-Rahim): they are like two names of the same root, and al-Rahim means the one who desires bestowal of favor upon creation, so their reference is the attribute of will (irada). And it was said: the giver of great favors and their details, so the reference then is an attribute of action. (Al-Malik) i.e., He honors whom He wills and humiliates whom He wills, and no one can humiliate whom He honors, so its reference is an attribute of action and a negative attribute. And it was said: its meaning is perfect power, so its reference is the attribute of power. (Al-Quddus) i.e., the one declared free from defects, and it was said: He whom imaginations and eyesights do not perceive, so it is a negative attribute in both aspects. (Al-Salam) i.e., the possessor of safety from imperfections absolutely in His essence, attributes, and actions, so it is a negative attribute. And it was said: its meaning is from Him and by Him is safety, i.e., He is the giver of safety in the beginning and the end, so it is an attribute of action. And it was said: He greets His creation, as He said: 'Peace, a word from a Merciful Lord' (Quran 36:58), so it is an attribute of speech. (Al-Mu'min) is the one who confirms Himself in what He has informed of, such as oneness, for example, in His statement: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He' (Quran 3:18), and confirms His messengers in what they have informed in their conveyance from Him, either by speech such as His statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' (Quran 48:29), so it is an attribute of speech; or He creates the miracle indicating the truthfulness of the messengers and the creation of the world on the observed order indicating oneness, so it is an attribute of action. And it was said: its meaning is the one who gives security to His believing servants from the great terror, either by His action and creating security and tranquility in them, so it returns to an attribute of action, or by His informing them of security from that, so it is an attribute of speech. (Al-Muhaymin) i.e., the Witness, and His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge, and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it was said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is al-Amin, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it was said: it means the Guardian (al-Hafiz). His statement: (due to widespread usage). It was said: there is no improbability in that it indicates some of them by considering the original meaning, as in nicknames and titles. Consider. His statement: (Al-Rahman, Al-Rahim): Al-Rahman is more comprehensive than Al-Rahim due to the increase in its form. Some considered the comprehensiveness in terms of quantity, as it was said: O Rahman of this world and Rahim of the Hereafter, because the mercy of this world encompasses the believer and the disbeliever, while the mercy of the Hereafter is specific to the believer. Some considered the comprehensiveness in terms of quality, interpreting Al-Rahman as the bestower of the favors of the Hereafter because they are all great, while the favors of this world are insignificant in comparison. And it was said: Al-Rahim is more comprehensive because the form fa'il is for innate attributes, but this is refuted by the terms 'sick' and 'ill'. Then Al-Rahman is among the prevailing attributes not used for other than Allah, and for this reason it is placed before Al-Rahim. And the statement of the Banu Hanifa to Musaylima the liar: 'Rahman of al-Yamama' is defiance and arrogance.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of several divine names. It begins by stating the general principle that naming God is based on revelation (tawqifiyya). Then it defines the name 'al-Qadir' (the Powerful) and notes that it returns to the attribute of power. It explains that the word 'Allah' was originally a description but became a proper name indicating perfection. Then it lists the names al-Rahman and al-Rahim, explaining that they refer to the attribute of will or an attribute of action. For al-Malik, it gives two interpretations: one that indicates honor and humiliation (action and negation) and another that indicates perfect power (attribute of power). Al-Quddus is a negative attribute. Al-Salam is either negative, active, or a speech attribute. Al-Mu'min is analyzed as confirming Himself and His messengers, either by speech or action, and also as giving security. Al-Muhaymin is the Witness, with interpretations as knowledge, speech, or guardianship. The marginal notes discuss the nuance between al-Rahman and al-Rahim, comparing their comprehensiveness and usage. The passage shows that each name has a precise meaning that determines its attribute category.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think al-Rahman and al-Rahim are synonymous or that divine names are arbitrary.
Correction: This passage shows they have distinct meanings (e.g., al-Rahman is more comprehensive) and that naming God is based on revelation, not human choice.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The names al-Rahman and al-Rahim, though both relate to mercy, are distinguished by their comprehensiveness and are linked to either the attribute of will or action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah by His names, do you truly believe that each name has a distinct and deep meaning that should shape your understanding of Him, or do you sometimes recite them without reflecting on their weight? What would change if you paused to consider the attribute behind each name before speaking it?
?
The lesson emphasizes that no name for God is invented by human reason; every name comes from revelation. Is there a place in your heart where you have attributed a human-like quality to Allah without scriptural basis? How can you root out such thoughts and submit to the names He has revealed?
?
Al-Rahman is a name that encompasses all creation, while al-Rahim is specific to believers. When you experience hardship or see suffering in the world, do you still recognize the all-encompassing mercy of al-Rahman, or do you doubt His mercy? How can you train your soul to see His mercy even in trials?

Divine Names and Their Attribute Categories (Part 2): al-Malik to al-Muhaymin
Definitions and attribute classifications for names al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the attribute classifications for the names al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin, and how each relates to attributes of action, negation, speech, or knowledge.

Core Idea
Each divine name reflects a unique aspect of Allah's attributes, whether of essence, action, speech, or negation.

This lesson continues the survey of divine names, examining five more: al-Malik, al-Quddus, al-Salam, al-Mu'min, and al-Muhaymin. The passage demonstrates the method of tracing each name back to its proper attribute domain, often offering multiple valid interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Analyze al-Malik
Notice that al-Malik is interpreted both as an attribute of action and negation (honouring and humiliating) and as an attribute of power (perfect power).
2
Understand al-Quddus
Read how al-Quddus is a negative attribute, indicating freedom from defects and imperceptibility.
Both interpretations lead to negation.
3
Examine al-Salam
Observe that al-Salam has three possible references: negative (freedom from imperfection), action (giving safety), and speech (greeting).
This shows how a single name can have multiple valid attribute categories.
4
Study al-Mu'min
Note how al-Mu'min involves confirmation (tasdiq) either by speech (divine statements) or by action (creating miracles). Also includes giving security.
5
Analyze al-Muhaymin
See how al-Muhaymin (the Witness) is traced to knowledge, speech, or guardianship.
The diversity of interpretations enriches understanding of the name.

The seventh observatory - the third purpose: Naming Him, exalted, with names is based on revelation (tawqifiyya). The Powerful over creation, so it returns to the attribute of power (qudra). And it was said: He is the one who only what He wills occurs. And it was said: He from whom valid obligation (taklif) is only from Him. So its reference in these two aspects is a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) and an attribute of action (sifa fi'liyya). And the correct view is that the word 'Allah', on the assumption that it was originally a description, has turned into a proper name (علم) indicating attributes of perfection due to widespread usage. (Al-Rahman) (Al-Rahim): they are like two names of the same root, and al-Rahim means the one who desires bestowal of favor upon creation, so their reference is the attribute of will (irada). And it was said: the giver of great favors and their details, so the reference then is an attribute of action. (Al-Malik) i.e., He honors whom He wills and humiliates whom He wills, and no one can humiliate whom He honors, so its reference is an attribute of action and a negative attribute. And it was said: its meaning is perfect power, so its reference is the attribute of power. (Al-Quddus) i.e., the one declared free from defects, and it was said: He whom imaginations and eyesights do not perceive, so it is a negative attribute in both aspects. (Al-Salam) i.e., the possessor of safety from imperfections absolutely in His essence, attributes, and actions, so it is a negative attribute. And it was said: its meaning is from Him and by Him is safety, i.e., He is the giver of safety in the beginning and the end, so it is an attribute of action. And it was said: He greets His creation, as He said: 'Peace, a word from a Merciful Lord' (Quran 36:58), so it is an attribute of speech. (Al-Mu'min) is the one who confirms Himself in what He has informed of, such as oneness, for example, in His statement: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He' (Quran 3:18), and confirms His messengers in what they have informed in their conveyance from Him, either by speech such as His statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' (Quran 48:29), so it is an attribute of speech; or He creates the miracle indicating the truthfulness of the messengers and the creation of the world on the observed order indicating oneness, so it is an attribute of action. And it was said: its meaning is the one who gives security to His believing servants from the great terror, either by His action and creating security and tranquility in them, so it returns to an attribute of action, or by His informing them of security from that, so it is an attribute of speech. (Al-Muhaymin) i.e., the Witness, and His being a witness is interpreted sometimes as knowledge, so it returns to the attribute of knowledge, and sometimes as confirmation by speech, so it returns to an attribute of speech. And it was said: the meaning of al-Muhaymin is al-Amin, i.e., the truthful in His speech, so it is an attribute of speech. And it was said: it means the Guardian (al-Hafiz). His statement: (due to widespread usage). It was said: there is no improbability in that it indicates some of them by considering the original meaning, as in nicknames and titles. Consider. His statement: (Al-Rahman, Al-Rahim): Al-Rahman is more comprehensive than Al-Rahim due to the increase in its form. Some considered the comprehensiveness in terms of quantity, as it was said: O Rahman of this world and Rahim of the Hereafter, because the mercy of this world encompasses the believer and the disbeliever, while the mercy of the Hereafter is specific to the believer. Some considered the comprehensiveness in terms of quality, interpreting Al-Rahman as the bestower of the favors of the Hereafter because they are all great, while the favors of this world are insignificant in comparison. And it was said: Al-Rahim is more comprehensive because the form fa'il is for innate attributes, but this is refuted by the terms 'sick' and 'ill'. Then Al-Rahman is among the prevailing attributes not used for other than Allah, and for this reason it is placed before Al-Rahim. And the statement of the Banu Hanifa to Musaylima the liar: 'Rahman of al-Yamama' is defiance and arrogance.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of several divine names. It begins by stating the general principle that naming God is based on revelation (tawqifiyya). Then it defines the name 'al-Qadir' (the Powerful) and notes that it returns to the attribute of power. It explains that the word 'Allah' was originally a description but became a proper name indicating perfection. Then it lists the names al-Rahman and al-Rahim, explaining that they refer to the attribute of will or an attribute of action. For al-Malik, it gives two interpretations: one that indicates honor and humiliation (action and negation) and another that indicates perfect power (attribute of power). Al-Quddus is a negative attribute. Al-Salam is either negative, active, or a speech attribute. Al-Mu'min is analyzed as confirming Himself and His messengers, either by speech or action, and also as giving security. Al-Muhaymin is the Witness, with interpretations as knowledge, speech, or guardianship. The marginal notes discuss the nuance between al-Rahman and al-Rahim, comparing their comprehensiveness and usage. The passage shows that each name has a precise meaning that determines its attribute category.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that each divine name has only one fixed attribute category.
Correction: The passage shows that many names (e.g., al-Salam, al-Mu'min, al-Muhaymin) have multiple valid interpretations, reflecting the richness of divine attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many different attribute categories are given for the name al-Salam?
A) One: negative only
B) Two: negative and action
C) Three: negative, action, and speech
D) Four: negative, action, speech, and knowledge

Key Takeaway
The diversity of interpretations for names like al-Salam and al-Mu'min shows that divine names can encompass multiple attribute domains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah as al-Salam, do you truly entrust your safety to Him in every aspect of your life, or do you rely on your own plans and precautions? What would change if you lived with the conviction that safety comes only from Him?
?
Al-Mu'min confirms His messengers through miracles like the Quran. After reading this lesson, do you find that your faith in the prophethood of Muhammad (ﷺ) rests on intellectual certainty rooted in the miracle of the Quran, or have you allowed doubts to linger? What step will you take today to strengthen your conviction?
?
The name al-Quddus means He is absolutely free from any defect. When you think about Allah, do you ever subconsciously attribute human limitations to Him—like forgetting, needing rest, or being affected by time? How can you purify your conception of Allah to reflect His true perfection?

Understanding al-'Aziz: Negative and Active Attributes
The author lists several interpretations of al-'Aziz and classifies them as negative or active attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the divine name al-'Aziz can be interpreted in multiple ways, leading to classifications as either a negative attribute or an attribute of action.

Core Idea
One divine name can carry both negative and active attribute meanings.

The name al-'Aziz is often translated as 'the Almighty' or 'the Mighty.' But classical scholars explored deeper meanings. This passage from al-Mawaqif presents several interpretations and classifies them as negative or active attributes. You'll see how the same name can be understood in different ways, each pointing to a different aspect of Allah's nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is structured as a list of interpretations.
2
Identify negative attribute interpretations
Look for interpretations that negate something about Allah: He has no father/mother, He does not descend, He is not aimed at, He has no like. These are negative attributes.
The author says the 'sum of all returns to a negative attribute.'
3
Identify active attribute interpretations
Find interpretations that describe actions: He punishes or rewards, He is powerful (giving victory). These return to attributes of action.
The author explicitly says 'so it returns to an attribute of action.'
4
Note the derivation and proverb
Observe how 'aziz is derived from 'izza (rarity, might) and the proverb 'Whoever is mighty, i.e., whoever has power and dominance, is overwhelming.'
This shows the linguistic root supports both interpretations.
5
Reflect on multiplicity of interpretations
Think about why a single name can have multiple valid interpretations and how they lead to different attribute categories.
This flexibility is common in divine names; context and usage determine the emphasis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العزيز قيل : ( معناه ( لا) أب له ولا أم وقيل : لا يحط عن منزلته ) ويقرب من هذا تفسيره بالذي لا يرام أو الذي لا يخالف أو الذي لا يخوف بالتهديد ( وقيل : لا مثل (له وهو بهذا المعنى وبالمعنى الأول مشتق عن عز الشيء يعز بالكسر في المستقبل إذا لم يكن له نظير، ومنه عز الطعام في البلد إذا تعذر وحاصل الكل يرجع إلى صفة سلبية . ( وقيل : يعذب من أراد وقيل عليه ثواب العاملين) فيرجع إلى صفة فعلية هي التعذيب أو الإثابة ) وقيل : القادر والعزة والقدرة ) والغلبة . (ومنه المثل : من عزبز ) أي من قدر وغلب سلب .
قوله : ( لايرام) أي لا ينال من رام يريم بمعنى برح.
قوله : ( وقيل : عليه ثواب العالمين كأنهم جعلوا العزيز بمعنى المعز المخبر.
Al-'Aziz. It was said: its meaning is that He has no father and no mother. And it was said: He does not descend from His station. Close to this is its interpretation as the one who is not aimed at, or the one who is not opposed, or the one who is not threatened. And it was said: He has no like. In this meaning and the first meaning, it is derived from 'izza al-shay' (the thing becomes rare) with kasra in the future tense, meaning it has no peer. From this comes scarcity of food in a town. The sum of all returns to a negative attribute. And it was said: He punishes whom He wills, and it was said: upon Him is the reward of the workers, so it returns to an attribute of action which is punishment or reward. And it was said: He is the Powerful, and might (al-'izza) is power and dominance. From this is the proverb: 'Whoever is mighty, i.e., whoever has power and dominance, is overwhelming.' His statement: (la yuram) i.e., it is not attained; from rama yarimu meaning to leave. His statement: (And it was said: upon Him is the reward of the worlds) as if they made al-'Aziz synonymous with al-Mu'izz (the Giver of honor) and al-Mukhbir (the Informer).
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition of the divine name al-'Aziz. The author lists multiple interpretations. First, some say it means 'He has no father or mother,' or 'He does not descend from His station,' or 'He cannot be aimed at, opposed, or threatened,' all of which are negative attributes (sifa salbiyya). Another interpretation says it means 'He has no like,' which also is negative and derived from rarity. Then he mentions an active interpretation: 'He punishes whom He wills and rewards workers,' which returns to an attribute of action. Another meaning is 'the Powerful,' where might is power and dominance, emphasizing the attribute of power. The marginal notes explain that 'la yurām' means unattainable, and that some interpret al-'Aziz as 'the Giver of honor' (al-Mu'izz) or 'the Informer' (al-Mukhbir), which would be active attributes. The passage illustrates that even a single name can have multiple valid interpretations that lead to different attribute categories.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume al-'Aziz only means 'Mighty' in a simple sense, without recognizing its possible negative attribute meanings.
Correction: The passage shows that al-'Aziz can be interpreted as both a negative attribute (e.g., having no like) and an active attribute (e.g., being powerful and rewarding).

Checkpoint
Which of the following interpretations of al-'Aziz is classified as an attribute of action (sifa fi'liyya)?
A) He has no like
B) He does not descend from His station
C) He punishes whom He wills and rewards workers
D) He has no father or mother

Key Takeaway
The divine name al-'Aziz can refer to either negative attributes (like uniqueness, inaccessibility) or active attributes (like power, reward), depending on how it is interpreted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is al-'Aziz', do you lean more toward His overwhelming power or His perfect uniqueness? Which aspect do you need to live by more today, and what would that look like in your next decision?
?
The name al-'Aziz reminds us that Allah cannot be opposed or threatened. Where in your life have you acted as if His commands can be negotiated or ignored? What will you change to show He truly is invincible?
?
Al-'Aziz also means He rewards and punishes. Do you ever forget His reward when you obey, or overlook His punishment when you sin? How will you keep both before your eyes tomorrow, without being paralyzed by fear or presumption?

The Names al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir: Interpretations and Attribute Categories
Definitions and classifications of al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple interpretations of the divine names al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir and how they map onto different categories of divine attributes (active, negative, relational, etc.).

Core Idea
The names al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir encompass a range of meanings, each pointing to different aspects of Allah's attributes.

The divine names are not always univalent; they can carry layers of meaning that reflect different aspects of Allah's perfection. In this passage, the author explores several interpretations of al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir, showing how each interpretation connects to a specific category of attributes—active, negative, relational, or combined. This lesson will guide you through these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the different interpretations listed for al-Jabbar and the brief treatment of al-Mutakabbir.
Pay attention to the phrase 'قيل' which introduces each interpretation.
2
Identify the interpretations of al-Jabbar
List each interpretation of al-Jabbar mentioned in the passage: reform, compulsion, unattainable, not caring, great (al-'Azim). Note the attribute category assigned to each.
Some interpretations have sub-variations, e.g., 'great' is explained in two ways.
3
Examine the connection to attribute categories
For each interpretation, see how the author classifies it: sifa fi'liyya (active), sifa salbiyya (negative), sifa idafiyya (relational), or combined. Understand the reasoning behind each classification.
The category depends on whether the meaning implies action, negation, relation, or affirmation.
4
Analyze the treatment of al-Mutakabbir
The passage says al-Mutakabbir has the same meaning as al-'Azim. Then it quotes al-Ghazali's definition: the one before whom everything is insignificant. Consider why this is a true attribute only for Allah.
Al-Ghazali's explanation ties the name to the concept of greatness and superiority.
5
Reflect on the significance of multiple interpretations
Think about why theologians provide multiple interpretations for a single name. How does this enrich our understanding of Allah? How does it prevent misunderstanding?
This passage shows that names like al-Jabbar are not limited to one facet of meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجبار قيل : من الجبر بمعنى الإصلاح (أي المصلح لأمور الخلائق فإنه جابر كل كسير (ومنه جبر العظم) أي أصلحه ( وقيل ) من الجبر ) بمعنى الإكراه ) يقال : جبره السلطان على كذا وأجبره إذا أكرهه ( أي يجبر خلقه ) ويحملهم ( على ما يريده فمرجعه على المعنيين صفة فعلية . ( وقيل : ) معناه ) منيع لاينال فإنه سبحانه وتعالى متعال عن أن تناله يد الأفكار أو يحيط به إدراك الأبصار ( ومنه نخلة جبارة ) إذا طالت وقصرت الأيدي عن أن تنال أعلاها، فمرجعه إلى صفة إضافية مع سلبية . وقيل : لا يبالي بما كان وبما لم يكن ( وقد يعبر عن هذا المعنى بأنه إذا لا يتمنى ما لا يكون ولا يلتهف على ما لم يكن فمرجعه إلى الصفات السلبية . ( وقيل : ( هو ( العظيم ) هكذا نقل عن ابن عباس، ثم فسر المصنف العظيم بقوله : ( أي انتفت عنه صفات النقص ) فمرجعه صفة سلبية ( وقيل : ( أي انتفى عنه تلك الصفات ) وحصل له جميع صفات ( الكمال ) فيرجع إلى الصفات السلبية والثبوتية معاً (المتكبر، قيل في معناه ما قيل في) معني (العظيم). وقال الغزالي رحمه الله : المتكبر المطلق هو الذي الكل يرى حقيراً بالإضافة إلى ذاته، فإن كانت هذه الرؤية صادقة كان التكبر حقاً وصاحبه محقاً ولا ذلك على الإطلاق إلا الله وإن كانت كاذبة كان التكبر باطلاً والمتكبر مبطلاً،
Al-Jabbar. It was said: from jabr meaning reform, i.e., the Reformer of the affairs of creation, for He mends every broken thing, from which is 'jabr al-'azm' (setting a bone). And it was said: from jabr meaning compulsion; it is said: the ruler compelled him to do such and such. i.e., He compels His creation and drives them to what He wills, so its reference in both meanings is an attribute of action. And it was said: its meaning is unattainable, not reached, for He, exalted, is above being reached by the hands of thoughts or encompassed by the perception of eyesights; from this is a tall palm tree (nakhla jabbara) when it is tall and hands fall short of reaching its top, so its reference is a relational attribute together with a negative attribute. And it was said: He does not care about what was and what was not, and this meaning may be expressed as: He does not wish for what is not and does not regret what was not, so its reference is negative attributes. And it was said: He is the Great (al-'Azim); thus it was narrated from Ibn 'Abbas. Then the author explained al-'Azim as: 'i.e., attributes of deficiency are negated from Him,' so its reference is a negative attribute. And it was said: 'i.e., those attributes are negated from Him and all attributes of perfection are attained for Him,' so it returns to negative and positive attributes together. (Al-Mutakabbir). It was said about its meaning what was said about the meaning of al-'Azim. And al-Ghazali, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The absolute Mutakabbir is He in relation to whom everything is seen as insignificant in relation to His essence. If this vision is true, then pride (takabbur) is true and its possessor is right, and this applies absolutely only to Allah. If it is false, then pride is false and the proud one is false.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the divine names al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir. For al-Jabbar, the author lists several interpretations: (1) from 'jabr' meaning reform, as He mends broken things, which is an attribute of action; (2) from 'jabr' meaning compulsion, also an attribute of action; (3) meaning unattainable, like a tall palm tree, which combines a relational attribute (idafiyya) with a negative attribute; (4) meaning He does not care about what was or was not, a negative attribute; (5) meaning the Great (al-'Azim), which is then interpreted as negating deficiencies (negative) or negating deficiencies and affirming perfections (both negative and positive). Then the name al-Mutakabbir is said to have the same meaning as al-'Azim. The author quotes al-Ghazali, who explains that the absolute Mutakabbir is He before whom everything is seen as insignificant; this is true only of Allah. The passage shows that these names are not univalent but carry multiple theological nuances and can refer to different attribute categories depending on the interpretation.

الجبار
المتكبر
جبر

Misconception: One might think al-Jabbar only means 'compeller' in a negative sense.
Correction: The passage shows al-Jabbar also means 'reformer' and 'unattainable', indicating positive and neutral meanings.

Checkpoint
According to the interpretation of al-Jabbar as 'unattainable like a tall palm tree', to what attribute category does it refer?
A) Attribute of action only
B) Negative attribute only
C) Relational attribute together with negative attribute
D) Positive attribute only

Key Takeaway
The names al-Jabbar and al-Mutakabbir have multiple valid interpretations, each highlighting a different aspect of Allah's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel pride in your achievements, do you ever pause to consider that any true greatness belongs only to Allah, and that your own perception of significance is false if it does not recognize His absolute transcendence? How can you train yourself to see your successes as mere manifestations of His jabr (reform and compulsion) rather than your own worth?
?
The name al-Jabbar includes the meaning of 'unattainable' – that Allah is beyond reach of thoughts and sight. In your daily spiritual practice, do you approach Allah with a sense of His overwhelming transcendence, or do you treat Him as if He is within your grasp? What would change if you meditated on His jabr as both mender and unattainable?
?
Al-Ghazali says that true takabbur is only for Allah, and our pride is false. Think of an area of your life where you secretly consider yourself superior to others. How does this lesson confront that delusion? What concrete step can you take today to embody humility in that specific area?

Divine Attributes
